href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">velocity</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0">\n<div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#ddf;text-align:center;">Scientists</div>\n<div class="NavContent plainlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;padding-top:0.35em;">\n<div class="hlist">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Newton</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Kepler</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jeremiah_Horrocks" title="Jeremiah Horrocks">Horrocks</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edmond_Halley" title="Edmond Halley">Halley</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Leonhard_Euler" title="Leonhard Euler">Euler</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jean_le_Rond_d%27Alembert" title="Jean le Rond d\'Alembert">d\'Alembert</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alexis_Clairaut" title="Alexis Clairaut">Clairaut</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph-Louis_Lagrange" title="Joseph-Louis Lagrange">Lagrange</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pierre-Simon_Laplace" title="Pierre-Simon Laplace">Laplace</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/William_Rowan_Hamilton" title="William Rowan Hamilton">Hamilton</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%A9on_Denis_Poisson" title="Sim\xc3\xa9on Denis Poisson">Poisson</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bernoulli" title="Daniel Bernoulli">Daniel Bernoulli</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Bernoulli" title="Johann Bernoulli">Johann Bernoulli</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Augustin-Louis_Cauchy" title="Augustin-Louis Cauchy">Cauchy</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;padding-top:0.15em;">\n<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n<ul>\n<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Classical_mechanics" title="Template:Classical mechanics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>\n<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Classical_mechanics" title="Template talk:Classical mechanics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>\n<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Classical_mechanics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Force" title="Force">force</a> is said to do <b>work</b> if, when acting, there is a <a href="/wiki/Displacement_(vector)" title="Displacement (vector)">displacement</a> of the point of application in the direction of the force. For example, when a ball is held above the ground and then dropped, the work done on the ball as it falls is equal to the weight of the ball (a force) multiplied by the distance to the ground (a displacement).</p>\n<p>Work transfers energy from one place to another or one form to another.</p>\n<p>The term <i>work</i> was introduced in 1826 by the French mathematician <a href="/wiki/Gaspard-Gustave_Coriolis" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaspard-Gustave Coriolis">Gaspard-Gustave Coriolis</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> as "weight <i>lifted</i> through a height", which is based on the use of early <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engines</a> to lift buckets of water out of flooded ore mines. The <a href="/wiki/SI_unit" class="mw-redirect" title="SI unit">SI unit</a> of work is the <a href="/wiki/Joule" title="Joule">joule</a> (J).</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Units"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Units</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Work_and_energy"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Work and energy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Constraint_forces"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Constraint forces</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Mathematical_calculation"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Mathematical calculation</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Work_done_by_a_variable_force"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Work done by a variable force</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Torque_and_rotation"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Torque and rotation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Work_and_potential_energy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Work and potential energy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Path_dependence"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Path dependence</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Path_independence"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Path independence</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Work_by_gravity"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Work by gravity</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Work_by_gravity_in_space"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Work by gravity in space</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Work_by_a_spring"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Work by a spring</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Work_by_a_gas"><span class="tocnumber">5.6</span> <span class="toctext">Work by a gas</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Work.E2.80.93energy_principle"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Work\xe2\x80\x93energy principle</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Derivation_for_a_particle_moving_along_a_straight_line"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Derivation for a particle moving along a straight line</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#General_derivation_of_the_work.E2.80.93energy_theorem_for_a_particle"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">General derivation of the work\xe2\x80\x93energy theorem for a particle</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Derivation_for_a_particle_in_constrained_movement"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Derivation for a particle in constrained movement</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#Vector_formulation"><span class="tocnumber">6.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Vector formulation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Tangential_and_normal_components"><span class="tocnumber">6.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Tangential and normal components</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Moving_in_a_straight_line_.28skid_to_a_stop.29"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Moving in a straight line (skid to a stop)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Coasting_down_a_mountain_road_.28gravity_racing.29"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Coasting down a mountain road (gravity racing)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Work_of_forces_acting_on_a_rigid_body"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Work of forces acting on a rigid body</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Units">Units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Units">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The SI unit of work is the <a href="/wiki/Joule" title="Joule">joule</a> (J), which is defined as the work expended by a force of one <a href="/wiki/Newton_(unit)" title="Newton (unit)">newton</a> through a displacement of one <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metre</a>.</p>\n<p>The dimensionally equivalent <a href="/wiki/Newton-metre" class="mw-redirect" title="Newton-metre">newton-metre</a> (N\xe2\x8b\x85m) is sometimes used as the measuring unit for work, but this can be confused with the unit newton-metre, which is the measurement unit of <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">torque</a>. Usage of N\xe2\x8b\x85m is discouraged by the <a href="/wiki/General_Conference_on_Weights_and_Measures" title="General Conference on Weights and Measures">SI authority</a>, since it can lead to confusion as to whether the quantity expressed in newton metres is a torque measurement, or a measurement of work.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Non-SI units of work include the <a href="/wiki/Erg" title="Erg">erg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Foot-pound_(energy)" title="Foot-pound (energy)">foot-pound</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Foot-poundal" title="Foot-poundal">foot-poundal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour" title="Kilowatt hour">kilowatt hour</a>, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Litre-atmosphere&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Litre-atmosphere (page does not exist)">litre-atmosphere</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Horsepower" title="Horsepower">horsepower-hour</a>. Due to work having the same <a href="/wiki/Dimensional_analysis" title="Dimensional analysis">physical dimension</a> as <a href="/wiki/Heat" title="Heat">heat</a>, occasionally measurement units typically reserved for heat or energy content, such as <a href="/wiki/Therm" title="Therm">therm</a>, <a href="/wiki/BTU" class="mw-redirect" title="BTU">BTU</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">Calorie</a>, are utilized as a measuring unit.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_and_energy">Work and energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Work and energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The work <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54a9c4c547f4d6111f81946cad242b18298d70b7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.446ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="W" /></span> done by a constant force of magnitude <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>F</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/545fd099af8541605f7ee55f08225526be88ce57" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.751ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="F" /></span> on a point that moves a displacement <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>s</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/01d131dfd7673938b947072a13a9744fe997e632" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.101ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="s" /></span> in a straight line in the direction of the force is the product</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mi>s</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=Fs}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b020230128c115d1b9e9cfbe6636985e98bbaf69" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.407ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle W=Fs}" /></span>.</dd>\n</dl>\n<p>For example, if a force of 10 newtons (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>F</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/545fd099af8541605f7ee55f08225526be88ce57" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.751ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="F" /></span> = 10 N) acts along a point that travels 2 meters (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>s</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/01d131dfd7673938b947072a13a9744fe997e632" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.101ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="s" /></span> = 2 m), then it does the work <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54a9c4c547f4d6111f81946cad242b18298d70b7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.446ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="W" /></span> = (10 N)(2 m) = 20 N m = 20 J. This is approximately the work done lifting a 1&#160;kg weight from ground level to over a person\'s head against the force of gravity. Notice that the work is doubled either by lifting twice the weight the same distance or by lifting the same weight twice the distance.</p>\n<p>Work is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>. The <a href="#Work-energy_principle">work-energy principle</a> states that an increase in the kinetic energy of a rigid body is caused by an equal amount of positive work done on the body by the resultant force acting on that body. Conversely, a decrease in kinetic energy is caused by an equal amount of negative work done by the resultant force.</p>\n<p>From <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion" title="Newton\'s laws of motion">Newton\'s second law</a>, it can be shown that work on a free (no fields), rigid (no internal degrees of freedom) body, is equal to the change in kinetic energy <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>K</mi>\n        <mi>E</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle KE}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/507bb8592e58edbb55ba67f37ce998e58047489f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.862ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="KE" /></span> of the velocity and rotation of that body,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- \xce\x94 --></mi>\n        <mi>K</mi>\n        <mi>E</mi>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\Delta KE.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fee3f13f31b6b8789817126396f1ee63342d4aae" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:12.021ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="W=\\Delta KE." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>The work of forces generated by a potential function is known as <a href="/wiki/Potential_energy" title="Potential energy">potential energy</a> and the forces are said to be <a href="/wiki/Conservative_force" title="Conservative force">conservative</a>. Therefore, work on an object that is merely displaced in a conservative force <a href="/wiki/Field_(physics)" title="Field (physics)">field</a>, without change in velocity or rotation, is equal to <i>minus</i> the change of potential energy <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>P</mi>\n        <mi>E</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle PE}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3618f41498880a11110aadc8495b704cebacb831" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.542ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle PE}" /></span> of the object,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- \xce\x94 --></mi>\n        <mi>P</mi>\n        <mi>E</mi>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=-\\Delta PE.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/747d29e1fce503ab050e247dcc5b606ef8e3a455" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:13.519ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="W=-\\Delta PE." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>These formulas show that work is the energy associated with the action of a force, so work subsequently possesses the <a href="/wiki/Dimensional_analysis" title="Dimensional analysis">physical dimensions</a>, and units, of energy. The work/energy principles discussed here are identical to Electric work/energy principles.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Constraint_forces">Constraint forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Constraint forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Constraint forces determine the movement of components in a system, constraining the object within a boundary (in the case of a slope plus gravity, the object is <i>stuck to</i> the slope, when attached to a taut string it cannot move in an outwards direction to make the string any \'tauter\'). Constraint forces ensure the velocity in the direction of the constraint is zero, which means the constraint forces do not perform work on the system.</p>\n<p>If the system <a href="/wiki/Virtual_work" title="Virtual work">doesn\'t change in time</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-4">[4]</a></sup> they eliminate all movement in the direction of the constraint, thus constraint forces do not perform work on the system, as the velocity of that object is constrained to be 0 parallel to this force, due to this force. This only applies for a single particle system. For example, in an <a href="/wiki/Atwood_machine" title="Atwood machine">Atwood machine</a>, the rope does work on each body, but keeping always the net virtual work null. There are, however, cases where this is not true.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>For example, the <a href="/wiki/Centripetal_force" title="Centripetal force">centripetal force</a> exerted <i>inwards</i> by a string on a ball in uniform <a href="/wiki/Circular_motion" title="Circular motion">circular motion</a> <i>sideways</i> constrains the ball to circular motion restricting its movement away from the center of the circle. This force does zero work because it is perpendicular to the velocity of the ball.</p>\n<p>Another example is a book on a table. If external forces are applied to the book so that it slides on the table, then the force exerted by the table constrains the book from moving downwards. The force exerted by the table supports the book and is perpendicular to its movement which means that this constraint force does not perform work.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnetic force">magnetic force</a> on a charged particle is <span class="nowrap"><b>F</b> = <i>q</i><b>v</b> \xc3\x97 <b>B</b></span>, where <i>q</i> is the charge, <b>v</b> is the velocity of the particle, and <b>B</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">magnetic field</a>. The result of a <a href="/wiki/Cross_product" title="Cross product">cross product</a> is always perpendicular to both of the original vectors, so <span class="nowrap"><b>F</b> \xe2\x8a\xa5 <b>v</b></span>. The <a href="/wiki/Dot_product" title="Dot product">dot product</a> of two perpendicular vectors is always zero, so the work <span class="nowrap"><i>W</i> = <b>F</b> \xe2\x8b\x85 <b>v</b> = 0</span>, and the magnetic force does not do work. It can change the direction of motion but never change the speed.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematical_calculation">Mathematical calculation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mathematical calculation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>For moving objects, the quantity of work/time (power) is calculated. Thus, at any instant, the rate of the work done by a force (measured in joules/second, or <b>watts</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/Scalar_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Scalar product">scalar product</a> of the force (a vector), and the velocity vector of the point of application. This scalar product of force and velocity is classified as instantaneous <a href="/wiki/Power_(physics)" title="Power (physics)">power</a>. Just as velocities may be integrated over time to obtain a total distance, by the <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_theorem_of_calculus" title="Fundamental theorem of calculus">fundamental theorem of calculus</a>, the total work along a path is similarly the time-integral of instantaneous power applied along the trajectory of the point of application.<sup id="cite_ref-Resnick_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resnick-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Work is the result of a force on a point that moves through a displacement. As the point moves, it follows a curve <b>X</b>, with a velocity <b>v</b>, at each instant. The small amount of work <i>\xce\xb4W</i> that occurs over an instant of time <i>dt</i> is calculated as</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>&#x03B4;<!-- \xce\xb4 --></mi>\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\delta W=\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} =\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2277d4841d3e704a83a98c202f65edf42acf962f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:22.278ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="\\delta W=\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} =\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt" /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where the <span class="nowrap"><b>F</b> \xe2\x8b\x85 <b>v</b></span> is the power over the instant <i>dt</i>. The sum of these small amounts of work over the trajectory of the point yields the work,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>1</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>1</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n            <mfrac>\n              <mrow>\n                <mi>d</mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>\n                </mrow>\n              </mrow>\n              <mrow>\n                <mi>d</mi>\n                <mi>t</mi>\n              </mrow>\n            </mfrac>\n          </mstyle>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot {\\tfrac {d\\mathbf {s} }{dt}}dt=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} ,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/24f9de9f3b829482f03e485fe3952a2afd47a3f0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:45.146ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="W=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot {\\tfrac {d\\mathbf {s} }{dt}}dt=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} ," /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where <i>C</i> is the trajectory from <b>x</b>(<i>t</i><sub>1</sub>) to <b>x</b>(<i>t</i><sub>2</sub>). This integral is computed along the trajectory of the particle, and is therefore said to be <i>path dependent</i>.</p>\n<p>If the force is always directed along this line, and the magnitude of the force is <i>F</i>, then this integral simplifies to</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>s</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{C}F\\,ds}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/db7d02ae3321f49301f20f492c5b7784881f4055" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:13.199ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="W=\\int _{C}F\\,ds" /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where <i>s</i> is displacement along the line. If <b>F</b> is constant, in addition to being directed along the line, then the integral simplifies further to</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>s</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <msub>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>s</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mi>s</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{C}F\\,ds=F\\int _{C}ds=Fs}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bb498cc293d618a52c688cec3f0760af9fc1ad0f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:29.913ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="W=\\int _{C}F\\,ds=F\\int _{C}ds=Fs" /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where <i>s</i> is the displacement of the point along the line.</p>\n<p>This calculation can be generalized for a constant force that is not directed along the line, followed by the particle. In this case the <a href="/wiki/Dot_product" title="Dot product">dot product</a> <span class="nowrap"><b>F</b> \xe2\x8b\x85 <i>d</i><b>s</b> = <i>F</i> cos <i>\xce\xb8</i> <i>ds</i></span>, where <i>\xce\xb8</i> is the angle between the force vector and the direction of movement,<sup id="cite_ref-Resnick_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resnick-5">[5]</a></sup> that is</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mi>s</mi>\n        <mi>cos</mi>\n        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- \xe2\x81\xa1 --></mo>\n        <mi>&#x03B8;<!-- \xce\xb8 --></mi>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} =Fs\\cos \\theta .}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f14d27e0f49e195993daf06d71b65dfff36b10b5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:26.044ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="W=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} =Fs\\cos \\theta ." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>In the notable case of a force applied to a body always at an angle of 90\xc2\xb0 from the velocity vector (as when a body moves in a circle under a central force), no work is done at all, since the cosine of 90 degrees is zero. Thus, no work can be performed by gravity on a planet with a circular orbit (this is ideal, as all orbits are slightly elliptical). Also, no work is done on a body moving circularly at a constant speed while constrained by mechanical force, such as moving at constant speed in a frictionless ideal centrifuge.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_done_by_a_variable_force">Work done by a variable force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Work done by a variable force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Calculating the work as "force times straight path segment" would only apply in the most simple of circumstances, as noted above. If force is changing, or if the body is moving along a curved path, possibly rotating and not necessarily rigid, then only the path of the application point of the force is relevant for the work done, and only the component of the force parallel to the application point <a href="/wiki/Velocity" title="Velocity">velocity</a> is doing work (positive work when in the same direction, and negative when in the opposite direction of the velocity). This component of force can be described by the scalar quantity called <i>scalar tangential component</i> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="1">\n          <mi>F</mi>\n          <mi>cos</mi>\n          <mo>&#x2061;<!-- \xe2\x81\xa1 --></mo>\n          <mi>&#x03B8;<!-- \xce\xb8 --></mi>\n        </mstyle>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle F\\cos \\theta }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bd0bf1e4d180b03434005cea0b8122048dc90bc7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.013ex; height:1.843ex;" alt="\\scriptstyle F\\cos \\theta " /></span>, where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="1">\n          <mi>&#x03B8;<!-- \xce\xb8 --></mi>\n        </mstyle>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle \\theta }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/635d7bc2a3756a9c19ec7ba7f9aacc676c8a324a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.778ex; height:1.843ex;" alt="\\scriptstyle \\theta " /></span> is the angle between the force and the velocity). And then the most general definition of work can be formulated as follows:</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><i>Work of a force is the line integral of its scalar tangential component along the path of its application point.</i></dd>\n<dd>If the force varies (e.g. compressing a spring) we need to use calculus to find the work done. If the force is given by F(x) (a function of x) then the work done by the force along the x-axis from a to b is:</dd>\n</dl>\n<p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <munderover>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>a</mi>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>b</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </munderover>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n          <mo mathvariant="bold" stretchy="false">(</mo>\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>\n          <mo mathvariant="bold" stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int \\limits _{a}^{b}\\mathbf {F(s)} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3a41c982b440b74561c6432095517de862898b37" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -4.005ex; width:16.987ex; height:9.343ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle W=\\int \\limits _{a}^{b}\\mathbf {F(s)} \\cdot d\\mathbf {s} }" /></span></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Torque_and_rotation">Torque and rotation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Torque and rotation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Couple_(mechanics)" title="Couple (mechanics)">force couple</a> results from equal and opposite forces, acting on two different points of a rigid body. The sum (resultant) of these forces may cancel, but their effect on the body is the couple or torque <b>T</b>. The work of the torque is calculated as</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">T</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mover>\n              <mi>&#x03C9;<!-- \xcf\x89 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- \xe2\x86\x92 --></mo>\n            </mover>\n          </mrow>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle dW=\\mathbf {T} \\cdot {\\vec {\\omega }}dt,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9fe0423bca1161c6f79908e87b8e1930f53b9ad9" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:14.53ex; height:2.676ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle dW=\\mathbf {T} \\cdot {\\vec {\\omega }}dt,}" /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where the <span class="nowrap"><b>T</b> \xe2\x8b\x85 <b>\xcf\x89</b></span> is the power over the instant <i>\xce\xb4t</i>. The sum of these small amounts of work over the trajectory of the rigid body yields the work,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>1</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">T</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mover>\n              <mi>&#x03C9;<!-- \xcf\x89 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- \xe2\x86\x92 --></mo>\n            </mover>\n          </mrow>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {T} \\cdot {\\vec {\\omega }}dt.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4fad5f3c9720e849224b4fa8b976ba6d7a91425c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:17.836ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="W=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {T} \\cdot {\\vec {\\omega }}dt." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>This integral is computed along the trajectory of the rigid body with an angular velocity \xcf\x89 that varies with time, and is therefore said to be <i>path dependent</i>.</p>\n<p>If the angular velocity vector maintains a constant direction, then it takes the form,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mover>\n              <mi>&#x03C9;<!-- \xcf\x89 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- \xe2\x86\x92 --></mo>\n            </mover>\n          </mrow>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mover>\n              <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n              <mo>&#x02D9;<!-- \xcb\x99 --></mo>\n            </mover>\n          </mrow>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">S</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\vec {\\omega }}={\\dot {\\phi }}\\mathbf {S} ,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/de6bd9f7c138e7ffe546858d68df524fd0a2f17a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.196ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="{\\vec {\\omega }}={\\dot {\\phi }}\\mathbf {S} ," /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where \xcf\x86 is the angle of rotation about the constant unit vector <b>S</b>. In this case, the work of the torque becomes,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math mathvariant="bold">T</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mover>\n              <mi>&#x03C9;<!-- \xcf\x89 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- \xe2\x86\x92 --></mo>\n            </mover>\n          </mrow>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>1</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">T</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi           </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>d</mi>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">T</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">S</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation _{C}\\mathbf {T} \\cdot \\mathbf {S} d\\phi ,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1823605641c9967028aa2ca5e0023e569b1ba29c" _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {T} \\cdot \\mathbf {S} {\\frac {d\\phi }{dt}}dt=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {T} \\cdot \\mathbf {S} d\\phi ," /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where <i>C</i> is the trajectory from <i>\xcf\x86</i>(<i>t</i><sub>1</sub>) to <i>\xcf\x86</i>(<i>t</i><sub>2</sub>). This integral depends on the rotational trajectory <i>\xcf\x86</i>(<i>t</i>), and is therefore path-dependent.</p>\n<p>If the torque <b>T</b> is aligned with the angular velocity vector so that,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {T} =\\tau \\mathbf {S} ,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/30b72ae28f4a7b461e35030e877fefe7eda7489f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.344ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="\\mathbf {T} =\\tau \\mathbf {S} ," /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>and both the torque and angular velocity are constant, then the work takes the form,<sup id="cite_ref-Young_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Young-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>1</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mi>&#x03C4;<!-- \xcf\x84 --></mi>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mover>\n              <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n              <mo>&#x02D9;<!-- \xcb\x99 --></mo>\n            </mover>\n          </mrow>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>&#x03C4;<!-- \xcf\x84 --></mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\tau {\\dot {\\phi }}dt=\\tau (\\phi _{2}-\\phi _{1}).}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/58aca0c124cf3832774e7183a52b9ee0a24b694b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:29.429ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="W=\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\tau {\\dot {\\phi }}dt=\\tau (\\phi _{2}-\\phi _{1})." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Work_on_the_lever_arm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Work_on_the_lever_arm.jpg/220px-Work_on_the_lever_arm.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Work_on_the_lever_arm.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="265" data-file-height="219" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Work_on_the_lever_arm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA force of constant magnitude and perpendicular to the lever arm</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>This result can be understood more simply by considering the torque as arising from a force of constant magnitude <i>F</i>, being applied perpendicularly to a lever arm at a distance <i>r</i>, as shown in the figure. This force will act through the distance along the circular arc <span class="nowrap"><i>s</i> = <i>r\xcf\x86</i></span>, so the work done is</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mi>s</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mi>r</mi>\n        <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=Fs=Fr\\phi .}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/355e2ef762e06b29d51d93290865421f53ac1798" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.379ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="W=Fs=Fr\\phi ." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Introduce the torque <span class="nowrap"><i>\xcf\x84</i> = <i>Fr</i></span>, to obtain</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mi>r</mi>\n        <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>&#x03C4;<!-- \xcf\x84 --></mi>\n        <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- \xcf\x95 --></mi>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=Fr\\phi =\\tau \\phi ,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c8369efe7b4f97ad2afb02e0fb60e305d7457804" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.135ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="W=Fr\\phi =\\tau \\phi ," /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>as presented above.</p>\n<p>Notice that only the component of torque in the direction of the angular velocity vector contributes to the work.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_and_potential_energy">Work and potential energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Work and potential energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The scalar product of a force <b>F</b> and the velocity <b>v</b> of its point of application defines the <a href="/wiki/Power_(physics)" title="Power (physics)">power</a> input to a system at an instant of time. Integration of this power over the trajectory of the point of application, <span class="nowrap"><i>C</i> = <b>x</b>(<i>t</i>)</span>, defines the work input to the system by the force.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Path_dependence">Path dependence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Path dependence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Therefore, the <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_work" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanical work">work</a> done by a force <b>F</b> on an object that travels along a curve <i>C</i> is given by the <a href="/wiki/Line_integral" title="Line integral">line integral</a>:</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>1</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {x} =\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ad41ea906a31472351d54b4d3a6c1644fef82757" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:29.943ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="W=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot d\\mathbf {x} =\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt," /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where <i>dx</i>(<i>t</i>) defines the trajectory <i>C</i> and <b>v</b> is the velocity along this trajectory. In general this integral requires the path along which the velocity is defined, so the evaluation of work is said to be path dependent.</p>\n<p>The time derivative of the integral for work yields the instantaneous power,</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>d</mi>\n              <mi>W</mi>\n            </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>d</mi>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>P</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\frac {dW}{dt}}=P(t)=\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} .}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f66dfa886e6b38066ef4a832dd1d3cdaf51d758f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:20.624ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="{\\frac {dW}{dt}}=P(t)=\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} ." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Path_independence">Path independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Path independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>If the work for an applied force is independent of the path, then the work done by the force is, by the <a href="/wiki/Gradient_theorem" title="Gradient theorem">gradient theorem</a>, the potential function evaluated at the start and end of the trajectory of the point of application. Such a force is said to be <a href="/wiki/Conservative_force" title="Conservative force">conservative</a>. This means that there is a potential function <i>U</i>(<b>x</b>), that can be evaluated at the two points <b>x</b>(<i>t</i><sub>1</sub>) and <b>x</b>(<i>t</i><sub>2</sub>) to obtain the work over any trajectory between these two points. It is tradition to define this function with a negative sign so that positive work is a reduction in the potential, that is</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle <mi>C</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi>\n            </mrow>\n            <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n            <msub>\n              <mi>t</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>1</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n            <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n            <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>U</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>t</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <mi>U</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>t</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{C}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {x} =\\int _{\\mathbf {x} (t_{1})}^{\\mathbf {x} (t_{2})}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {x} =U(\\mathbf {x} (t_{1}))-U(\\mathbf {x} (t_{2})).}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c2f561642e3b3969b5675183d8bd1c571bebf0b3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" \\cdot \\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {x} =U(\\mathbf {x} (t_{1}))-U(\\mathbf {x} (t_{2}))." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>The function <i>U</i>(<b>x</b>) is called the <a href="/wiki/Potential_energy" title="Potential energy">potential energy</a> associated with the applied force. Examples of forces that have potential energies are gravity and spring forces.</p>\n<p>In this case, the <a href="/wiki/Gradient" title="Gradient">gradient</a> of work yields</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow     <mrow>\n          <mo>(</mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mfrac>\n              <mrow>\n                <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- \xe2\x88\x82 --></mi>\n                <mi>U</mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mrow>\n                <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- \xe2\x88\x82 --></mi>\n                <mi>x</mi>\n              </mrow>\n            </mfrac>\n          </mrow>\n          <mo>,</mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mfrac>\n              <mrow>\n                <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- \\nabla W=-\\nabla U=-\\left({\\frac {\\partial U}{\\partial x}},{\\frac {\\partial U}{\\partial y}},{\\frac {\\partial U}{\\partial z}}\\right)=\\mathbf {F} ,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/992dd2e43776610739af8c23ec67b3856c2e8d4c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:41.237ex; height:6.176ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle \\nabla W=-\\nabla U=-\\left({\\frac {\\partial U}{\\partial x}},{\\frac {\\partial U}{\\partial y}},{\\frac {\\partial U}{\\partial z}}\\right)=\\mathbf {F} ,}" /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>and the force <b>F</b> is said to be "derivable from a potential."<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Because the potential <i>U</i> defines a force <b>F</b> at every point <b>x</b> in space, the set of forces is called a <a href="/wiki/Force_field_(physics)" title="Force field (physics)">force field</a>. The power applied to a body by a force field is obtained from the gradient of the work, or potential, in the direction of the velocity <b>V</b> of the body, that is</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>P</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2207;<!-- \xe2\x88\x87 --></mi>\n        <mi>U</mi>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle P(t)=-\\nabla U\\cdot \\mathbf {v} =\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} .}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/39cdfc586392f80d5ef3b7de7d2989289b475e9e" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:24.784ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle P(t)=-\\nabla U\\cdot \\mathbf {v} =\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} .}" /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_by_gravity">Work by gravity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Work by gravity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:170px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Work_of_gravity_F_dot_d_equals_mgh.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/Work_of_gravity_F_dot_d_equals_mgh.JPG" width="168" height="138" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="168" data-file-height="138" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Work_of_gravity_F_dot_d_equals_mgh.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nGravity <span class="nowrap"><i>F</i> = <i>mg</i></span> does work <span class="nowrap"><i>W</i> = <i>mgh</i></span> along any descending path</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In the absence of other forces, gravity results in a constant downward acceleration of every freely moving object. Near Earth\'s surface the acceleration due to gravity is <span class="nowrap"><i>g</i> = 9.8&#160;m\xe2\x8b\x85s<sup>\xe2\x88\x922</sup></span> and the gravitational force on an object of mass <i>m</i> is <span class="nowrap"><b>F</b><sub>g</sub> = <i>mg</i></span>. It is convenient to imagine this gravitational force concentrated at the center of mass of the object.</p>\n<p>If an object is displaced upwards or downwards a vertical distance <span class="nowrap"><i>y</i><sub>2</sub> \xe2\x88\x92 <i>y</i><sub>1</sub></span>, the work <i>W</i> done on the object by its weight mg is:</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>y</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>y</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>F</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>g</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- \xce\x94 --></mi>\n        <mi>y</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <mi>m</mi>\n        <mi>g</mi>\n        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- \xce\x94 --></mi>\n        <mi>y</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=F_{g}(y_{2}-y_{1})=F_{g}\\Delta y=-mg\\Delta y}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b3cdc03e07f1c8155b2bee2103f65a004f0f79ed" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:37.164ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="W=F_{g}(y_{2}-y_{1})=F_{g}\\Delta y=-mg\\Delta y" /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>where <i>F<sub>g</sub></i> is weight (pounds in imperial units, and newtons in SI units), and \xce\x94<i>y</i> is the change in height <i>y</i>. Notice that the work done by gravity depends only on the vertical movement of the object. The presence of friction does not affect the work done on the object by its weight.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_by_gravity_in_space">Work by gravity in space</span><span W=-\\int _{\\mathbf {r} (t_{1})}^{\\mathbf {r} (t_{2})}{\\frac {GMm}{r^{3}}}\\mathbf {r} \\cdot d\\mathbf {r} =-\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}{\\frac {GMm}{r^{3}}}\\mathbf {r} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/05674aa6446ec9efa3490163a3b9eeb1ebf3f976" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.838ex; width:50.673ex; height:6.843ex;" alt="W=-\\int _{\\mathbf {r} (t_{1})}^{\\mathbf {r} (t_{2})}{\\frac {GMm}{r^{3}}}\\mathbf {r} \\cdot d\\mathbf {r} =-\\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}{\\frac {GMm}{r^{3}}}\\mathbf {r} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt." /></span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Notice that the position and velocity of the mass <i>m</i> are given that</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n The negative sign follows the convention that work is gained from a loss of potential energy.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_by_a_spring">Work by a spring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Work by a spring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg/170px-Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg.png" width="170" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg/255px-Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg/340px-Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="278" data-file-height="429" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Analogie_ressorts_contrainte.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nForces in springs assembled in parallel</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Consider a spring that exerts a horizontal force <span class="nowrap"><b>F</b> = (\xe2\x88\x92<i>kx</i>, 0, 0)</span> that is proportional to its deflection in the <i>x</i> direction independent of how a body moves. The work of this spring on a body moving along the space with the curve <span class="nowrap"><b>X</b>(<i>t</i>) = (<i>x</i>(<i>t</i>), <i>y</i>(<i>t</i>), <i>z</i>(<i>t</i>))</span>, is calculated using its velocity, <span class="nowrap"><b>v</b> = (<i>v</i><sub>x</sub>, <i>v</i><sub>y</sub>, <i>v</i><sub>z</sub>)</span>, to obtain</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle <mn>0</mn>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>t</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi  <mi>x</mi>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>v</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>x</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>t</mi>\n </mrow>\n        <mi>k</mi>\n        <msup>\n          <mi>x</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msup>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{0}^{t}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt=-\\int _{0}^{t}kxv_{x}dt=-{\\frac {1}{2}}kx^{2}.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ae7e7a0e814645c626066f3f2ce845cb0697bc81" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:43.313ex; height:6.176ex;" alt="W=\\int _{0}^{t}\\mathbf {F} \\cdot \\mathbf {v} dt=-\\int product of the distance <i>x</i> and the x-velocity, <i>xv</i><sub>x</sub>, is (1/2)<i>x</i><sup>2</sup>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_by_a_gas">Work by a gas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Work_(physics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Work by a gas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<dl>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>W</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>a</mi>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>b</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mi>P</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>V</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle W=\\int _{a}^{b}{P}dV}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ceac3c0def499fb2a60f691d1a964aa686186192" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex;
